<rating>3</rating>< Text>
Security guards in the front were a bit rude when they were asking for my ID.

Had a party of about 8 people and we got the biggest room because it was all they had left. The room was spacious and came with a lot of mics. There were two TVs. One main screen big screen and another TV in the back displaying the same thing. It also came with a small stage with a standing mic, which was funny. The staff member showed us the room and showed us how to use the system. He took his time explaining everything.

The navigation of sounds were pretty easy to use. It was a bit annoying typing in/ searching songs, but they had all the songs we wanted-- lots of throwbacks plus new songs! Which is great!

The sound system was.. a little obnoxious. Kinda wasn't clear/ great. I'm sure we could have adjusted the volume, but didn't know how and didn't bother because we were only there for one hour

Water bottles cost like $2.75 or something. Why can't water just be free.. I guess that's how they make money isn't it?

Interaction with staff was minimal. They never came to check in and I wish they did! Service could've been better. They only came in once to give us our beer and that was it. Also wished they had a variety selection of drinks. But all they had was beer and sake/wine or something. $25/ person for one hour.< /Text>

< review>
I've been and seen a lot of karaoke bars. This one stands out among all that i have experienced. There have different sized rooms and i think their biggest one from what I've seen can accommodate up to 20 people comfortably. Without leaving, you can order food and drinks by just pressing the service button along the walls- someone will come to take your orders.

They have a huge selection that includes the latest releases in various languages, and they have a live concert version of the music, too. Parking was rather easy for me. There is ground level parking and street parking all around the building. There is also parking underground. You do not need to pay for parking.

They are also other surrounding businesses that you might want to order from or a place to hangout to have breaks. They are open late as well.
The restroom is clean, well maintained and easily accessible. The staff are all very friendly. I do plan to come back again.< /review>

< Rate>
5< /Rate>
< Text>
This is a favorite hike for our family with great views of Laguna Beach! There are two approaches and one is more difficult than the other. The south trailhead is our favorite, but is more difficult. It begins in a residential neighborhood and ascends something like 600-650 feet in a matter of a 1/4-1/2 mile. With kids, this might be a little difficult. The other approach is from the East and is much more moderate because you park on top of a hill. When you come to the fork in the trail near the end, keep right to ascend to the tallest part of the peak. The views are excellent and there is a bench at the top. Beware of the sharp cliffs with the kids!<//Text>

<gmap_id>0x80c0825007eb15f1:0xdcdcda0bbf450349< /gmap_id>< Name>
Candace R<//Name>
<Time>1531814107431</Time>< review>
I will run out of space before I can accurately describe all that is Cerro Gordo. This is an amazing place. There are endless facts and tidbits of information for each step you take in Cerro Gordo. There is still a home standing, that was built in 1862. This house is known to be extremely haunted by at least 3 known subjects. You can feel the heaviness in some spots on the property.

The hotel is stunning. You can feel the way things must have been during the peak of mining here. The building is beginning to become an issue. The second floor is not accessible, due to the floor, or ceiling on the first floor, sagging. That you can probably acredit to miners placing sandbags completely around their beds to avoid being hit with a stray bullets in this once lawless town.

Fair warning to anyone who does not have a good sense of driving, or is inexperienced in climbing elevation quickly in a vehicle. You will overheat any vehicle if you are not cautious about overworking your engine. Turn off your A/C, roll down your windows, keep it moving going up, and in low gear going down. A bit of dust won't hurt, but don't drive your beloved car if you don't want it to get a little dirty. Even the toughest of vehicles will strain in this environment.

(Depicted in the photos, you can see what looks like a bucket suspended hundreds of feet in the air from a cable. This bucket is still full of ore. If you brave the trip, there is a drone snapped photo of the inside of the bucket that is very cool.)< /review>

<Rate>5< /Rate>< text>
There's just not that many places left where you find a huge trove of authentic history still in the wild. The folks here were friendly and open to showing people around, and the photo opportunities were many. For a nominal fee guided tours were available. The remote mountains there were uncrowded, even on a beautiful fall weekend. Come prepared for high elevation weather and remote desert beauty. Add a four wheel drive vehicle and enjoy a playground of off-road trails. Worth the drive.< /text>

<Time>1529030242367<//Time><rate>5< /rate>< Review>
It was 1993 when we had our first of many trips to Cerro Gordo.  We met Jodie and Mike and had a wonderful friendship with them.  Spent many nights in the bunkhouse and made trips to the outhouse and saw so many stars it was hard to go back to bed.  We helped rebuild a couple of the buildings.  We made it up the mountain just a few months before Mike passed away - he was so excited to show us the "theatre".  Our beloved Jodie was laid to rest above the town.   It was amazing to hear her tell us the history of Cerro Gordo.<//Review>

< UserId.>
103530993878436795307<//UserId.>
<user_name>Micheal Espinola</user_name><Date>1473318114023< /Date><rate>5</rate>< Review>
Preface: Cerro Gordo is a private ghost town that is maintained by a caretaker (Robert).  It's a public road to get there, but the land and property is private.  It's highly recommended to make arrangements with Robert for when you would like to come up and see the town, so that he can be available.  Otherwise, you are trespassing - and you won't get to go inside any of the buildings.

Words can't describe what a treasure of a ghost town this is.  Although its relatively small, Robert the caretaker is the true gem hidden up in these mountains.  He is a wealth of information regarding the history of the town and the area in general.  He will walk and talk you through most of the property and is not shy to allow you to touch the history around you.  Bodie is larger and does have the stamp mill (extra $ to tour it), but Cerro Gordo has Robert - and he is amazing.

You can also rent rooms up there to stay, in the buildings of the ghost town!  You'll have to get the full details from Robert.

Robert is currently doing the tours for free, but its customary to give him some money for his efforts.  It's worth it - He's worth it!  Also, he doesn't have running water up there, so its also a kindness to bring up a jug of water.  He will greatly appreciate it as it will inevitably save him a trip at some point.< /Review>

We were on a road trip of the west coast of America and were driving between las Vegas and bishop, and noticed a sign that said " historical sites ". We had a jeep patriot and began curiously driving up the gravel road. We got about 4 mile in and I honestly went to turn around as I thought it was going to be a dead end. My mate persuaded me to carry on and with caution I crept up another 2 mile with the cliff edges next to me and stumbled across one of the most spectacular places I have seen. I was roaming around looking at the fabulous abandoned buildings when a man offered to show us around. He was the caretaker and lived with his wife up there. No mains water, no post, and 6 mile from civilization. We had a personal guided tour and the history he knew was second to none. To stand up there and look down at the desert below is something I will never forget. It is breathtakingly beautiful. Please go and see for yourself. The buildings are stunning, the view is amazing and you can get a personal guided tour from a man with a wealth of knowledge. < Text>
The well preserved remnants of this mining town provide an intense glimpse of a past way of life in extremely adverse conditions, nestled near the saddle of a steep ridge. The caretaker is a breed apart and has great stories. I came here with an off-roading group and he gave us a tour through several buildings and told us about the history of the place along with mining practices. It's possible to arrange to stay overnight in the bunkhouse, and groups can reserve the inn for events.<//Text>

< text>
One of my favorite places in Eastern California. I drove my Nissan Cube up the mountain with no problems, except when the truck was coming down the hill and I had to back down the road for a quarter mile with a several hundred foot drop on one side. The road up to Cerro Gordo is criss crossed by old tram lines and towers. At the top of the mountain the amazing town of Cerro Gordo still stands. This town and it's mines helped build Los Angeles and it's worth reading about if you're a Californian. The hotel still operates by reservation only last I checked. Really want to stay a night in the oldest, original standing hotel east of the Sierras, the American Hotel.< /text>

<text>(Translated by Google) An authentic ghost town.

To get to the ghost town, you have to take a small fork on a stony track of about 8 miles with a good elevation. It took us about 45 minutes and could suggest that we were on the wrong route. It is better to rent a 4x4 or an SUV to venture there and do it preferably only in good weather.

Once there, it is an isolated and authentic place that holds out its arms to us. We met Robert who lives up there and took care of maintaining the site. Very friendly, we had a little chat and he opened the doors to one or the other building (period boutique, hotel / bar ...). We were then able to visit the site while Robert went about his business.

With mild weather it is easy to take very nice photos because the brightness is excellent, even if it is quite cool (because of the altitude). In the same way it will allow to have an excellent view on the plain.

It feels like a real ghost village (only the sound of the wind is heard). Few tourists (less than a dozen tourists a week during the good weeks), which makes it a little touristy but essential place.

(Translated by Google) At first, we were very worried that our car (Dodge Grand Caravan) would pack the dirt road. We did not know if it was worth it. Only 7 miles, can not be so wild. BUT: 1000 meters difference in height were the hammer ... Without climate and heating fully on, only so we managed it, without the engine overheated even more. Arriving at an incredible 2,400 meters, the air was incredibly clear and cool. Robert, the only inhabitant of the old village, immediately "found us". Next to him live only 7 wild rabbits, a small dog, owls and Nighthawks, an (unloved) skunk and bats.
We did not expect anyone to live here, he immediately offered us the tour of the abandoned buildings. Thousands of original Wild West timepieces are on the shelves, tools for mining ores with silver and copper are there to touch. Robert said it was a "living museum" - and with pride. The mine tunnels are also accessible, Robert regularly brings items up with him. He knows his way around, after all, he was once active here and was looking for silver.
He and a friend try to preserve the buildings and partly to rebuild them.
Up to 2000 (!!!) people used to live in the city. Connection to electricity came only in 1916. At times there was even running water.
For us, this trip was exciting, sweaty but deeply impressive. Thanks to Robert!
Next time we come with a bag full of Lindt chocolate and a box of wine and stay with Robert overnight to experience the magnificent starry sky. Worth a journey and a REAL INSIDER TIP!

<username>Sara Kwan<//username><date>1557448844129</date>< rating>

<review>Excellent experience through and through. All the staff were so helpful and caring, making the day of surgery less stressful. Alison Gordon was the surgeon who did my Lasik, she talked me through the entire procedure so nothing was a surprise. You get the option of taking a Valium to calm any nerves during the procedure. The procedure itself was essential painless, with exception of the creation of the flap, you feel slight pressure as if you pushed on your eyelids. I did have pain for about 2 hours after the procedure but it was similar to how it feels when you're cutting an onion, nothing extraordinary. < text>
From my very first visit, my experience was amazing.  The front office staff, the scheduling coordinator, the medical technicians, my doctor, Dr. Echegoyen and Dr. Pust who filled in for my follow up, everyone was friendly, helpful, caring, compassionate and concerned with my comfort and well being.

Just for some background on me, I have had 5 surgeries in one of my eyes.  I had multiple retinal detachments about 7 yrs ago and needed surgeries to repair, and then needed follow up surgery and eventually cataract surgery.  So, I have spent a lot of time in eye specialists offices.  This time, I needed cataract surgery in my other eye.  Very basic procedure.  The difference with Dr. Echegoyen was that he didn't try to up sell me on the procedure, unlike the two other surgeons I saw previous to coming to Gordon Schanzlin.  Both told me they couldn't do my monovision procedure (when 1 eye is for distance and 1 is for reading), without charging me extra, and then also insisted that I likely wouldn't have a good outcome without using all the very latest equipment, even though standard cataract surgery has been extremely successful for decades.  Dr. Echegoyen immediately put me at ease and assured me this was a very doable situation.  The surgical center was great, (it was at Grossmont), and the nurses were second to none.  Dr. E was there at exactly my scheduled surgery time, and I barely had any time to be anxious.

I also can't forget Kay Nicholas, who is the scheduling coordinator, although she is so much more than that.  My original surgery was schedule for a different surgical center, which suddenly experienced a management shift, meaning they had to renegotiate their insurance contracts.  That meant not only could I not go there, but everyone else who was scheduled couldn't either, unless they were paying out of pocket.  She spent what I am sure was countless hours rescheduling me and all of the other patients, which included finding slots in other surgical centers.  I ended up with a surgical slot only 1 week later than my original one!  True magic.  She also went out of her way to make sure I had my paperwork and medications, as well as finding out what my deductible would be for the surgical center.

My incredibly positive experience wiped out all of the long hours and frustrating interactions of eye appointments past.  Thank you Dr. Echegoyen and Gordon Schanzlin New Vision Institute for taking such good care of me!< /text>

Stellar experience from beginning to end.  This medical office is clean and well appointed with modern amenities. The staff is very friendly, courteous, and professional.  The physicians go out of their way to explain the procedures and to calm anxious nerves.  I received LASIK vision correction surgery at this location yesterday. But the staff explained everything to me as the procedure progressed and told me what I could expect as far as pain and how the healing process should go. I am truly thankful for all the little details the Schanzlin crew put into making sure my LASIK procedure went off without a hitch, even the lovely bouquet of flowers!! < text>
TL;DR: LASIK with Dr. Bavand and the Gordon Institute was easily the best decision of my life despite having many hesitations and a very high prescription. GO HERE!

Wow... where to begin. I'm in my mid 20's but have had horrible vision for years. Terrible astigmatism, irregular cornea shape etc. I had to get custom made contact lenses from Australia to fit my eyes, then had to switch to hard lenses since those stopped working. I could not do anything without glasses or contacts.

I was told when I was younger that I wouldn't be able to get LASIK due to the risk of complications with my high prescription. I did some reading and saw that the technology seemed to have progressed a lot in the last 5 years or so. I figured I would go to some consultations just to see what was out there. In the beginning, I figured more likely than not I would not end up getting the procedure.

I went to 4-5 different LASIK consultations in the San Diego area (La Jolla Lasik, Motwani, Dr. Pham, Gordon Schanzlin, and possibly another one I forget). All of these places have good review and the staff seem competent. However, after my own research and discussions with the surgeons, I decided I wanted the best technology I could find (EX500 laser with Contoura vision) which narrowed down the options to Gordon and Motwani.

Motwani seems VERY competent. He has a number of scientific publications on protocols for extreme cases, he seems very knowledgable. He does have a number of lawsuits opened against him, I do not know the details. Regardless, I have little doubt he is very good at what he does. However, his office and staff came across as putting more pressure on to sell their service, and they very quickly wanted to get me into surgery.

Gordon was different. Again, they seem very competent and have a history of breakthroughs in vision corrective surgery, similar to Motwani. However, they were very thorough and performed many more diagnostic tests to ensure I was a good candidate. Additionally, they insisted on repeating these tests at a later date to ensure my eyes were stable. I met with Dr. Bavand Youssefzadeh (or Dr. B, as I call him now) before my surgery. He was very easy going but professional and put me at ease, answering all of my questions. Ultimately, I felt much more comfortable with the procedures of Gordon Institute and with Dr. Bavand.

I cannot stress enough the importance of being comfortable with your surgeon. It is remarkable how quickly the procedure goes. You go into the office, get your prescription checked, take a Valium, and wait for a little bit. You get some numbing eye drops, and lie on the operating table. Then, you see the laser. Shortly afterwards, it comes close to your eye, you feel lots of pressure (uncomfortable, but well worth it), and your vision blacks out. Then, vision goes in and out of extremely blurry to somewhat there. There are lots of tears and things going on, and the other eye gets operated on. Then you go to another laser that finishes the job.

The procedure itself is pretty nerve-wrecking. This is part of why I am so happy with choosing surgery with Dr. Bavand and cannot stress the importance of being comfortable with your doctor and able to trust him. The procedure is so foreign, unlike any other experience, that you are truly at the "mercy" of the technology and the surgeon, so you must be able to trust them. D. Bavand knew I was nervous going into the procedure, and I asked him to talk me through the procedure to keep me at ease, which he happily did. He let me know what was going on, what would happen, and assured me throughout the procedure that everything was going great.

I am now writing this less than 24 hours after my surgery with better than perfect 20/15 vision. My eyes are pain free. This is easily the best decision I have ever made in my life, I almost feel like a new person. I can offer no higher recommendation and do not possess the proper vocabulary to adequately praise the Gordon Institute and Dr. Bavand personally.< /text>

< review>
Dr. Schanzlin and Dr. Elizabeth Viriya were outstanding care providers.

Wait time: 1.5 hour consultation visit, about an hour at the surgery center total (10 minute surgery), and 15 minute post-op visit. Excellent.

Bedside manner: I chose not to take the Valium so I was still a little nervous during the surgery, and both doctors told me what was about to happen before it did. They kept talking to me the whole time as I requested. ("Now your vision should be blurry, now 8 seconds of pressure, now your eye should be able to see and feel better...")

Actual results: I see 20/20 and 20/15 in right and left eye, respectively, 1 day after the procedure. I had a little pain and self-treated with Advil, didn't even need the Vicodin. If you work in a hospital tell them and they will give you different antibiotics for MRSA coverage. Now I have a bit of sandy-eye sensation but nothing more and no pain!

The Surgery: it felt like pressure (not pain but still discomfort) for about 20 seconds per eye on the first laser, and nothing on the second laser. It's a little freaky to see your vision go black in each eye but this is entirely normal and quickly your vision comes back. I had bad pain only for 2 hours after the surgery and then just sandy-eye sensation. And I refused the Vicodin for personal reasons so I'm sure the "bad pain" wouldn't have been that bad if you just take the drug they give you.

In summary...would recommend this office and these physicians to literally anyone who asks. As a medical student myself I am very careful about my own healthcare and especially surgical needs, so you can assure yourself that someone more neurotic than you (me) liked this place very much.</review>

With more and more restaurants starting to resume services at 100% capacity, you are given an opportunity to finally sit inside the restaurant or outdoors in their makeshift  EZ-Up tents. I came with a friend for dinner and the service was great, probably because there wasn't that many guests inside the restaurant; not complaining though!

As you enter the restaurant, they workers do not take your temperature or take your name down anymore. I think at this point, most people who go out to eat have been vaccinated and they no longer want to waste time to contact trace. Whether you like it or not, the workers are still masked up and most of them have gloves on just as a safety precaution for them.

My friend and I both ordered grilled chicken steak with their black pepper sauce with a side of veggies and pasta. As other reviewers have mentioned, you're able to substitute pasta for rice or fries. It's always been my go to HK Style dish at any HK Cafe's in the SGV. Weirdly enough, I don't ever order that dish when I visit relatives back in Hong Kong. Not long after we ordered, the food came out steaming hot, literally steaming, so you know it wasn't sitting on the counter waiting for a server to take it to us. The chicken was cooked perfectly, especially how they made the skin extra crispy. Don't get your hopes up during their peak hours because it'll most likely be crowded and the server busy running around. However, please be courteous to the servers because they've had it hard this past year and they're doing their best to catch up and do their jobs.

If you're ever in the area, definitely check out Baccali's because you won't be disappointed with the variety of choices on their menu.</text><rate>4</rate>< userid>

<time>1597617082583</time>< Text>
Passed by here many times and haven‚Äôt had a chance to try them out. Heard a lot from my friends raving about the foods. We finally decided to give a try this Saturday on our way to Ventura.

With Covid-19, the Cafe offers outdoor seatings. Under the 110F temperature, we ordered the famous ice lemon tea immediately after we were seated. It really helped to cool us down.

Because we were in a hurry, we ordered a
Char kway teow (ÁÇíÁ≤øÊù°) and a pan fried chicken and Steak dishes. The chicken and steak came out first. We chowed down the meat pretty fast as they were very tasty. I think this dish came out better than the ones from most of the Hong Kong Cafe in SV. The Char Kway Teow came out much later as the kitchen was overwhelmed by take out orders during lunch time. When the dish finally came, we enjoyed the curry fun. I would say the flavor was very close to the ones I had in Hong Kong or in Singapore.

I heard this place opens for breakfast too. We‚Äôll be back to try out their breakfast. From what I have seen from the Yelp reviews, the foods seemed to be very good. Looking forward to the next visit.</Text>

<review>Baccali is a local favorite. The restaurant offers a large and varied menu popular in Hong Kong and the Canton area of southern China. There are Western style dishes featuring a mix of their house chicken and steak, fish or lamb. Those come with a choice of pasta, rice and vegetable. The majority of the menu comprises Chinese dishes, with a section of Malaysian and Indonesian fare. Like a lot of restaurants of this genre (they are popular in this area) the food tends to be high on the salt content. So if you care, tell them to limit it. Additionally, unless you're dead set on eating Western food..skip it and get Chinese. It tends to be better prepared. The only Western item they make fairly well is their house chicken. The eel feed rice and their beef chow fun are both good here by the way.<//review><response>None<//response>< user_name>

<Name>Dereck S</Name>< date>
1552377681216<//date>
<rate>3< /rate>< text>
My wife and I are hooked on the Souldon "Chicken Steak".You can ask for white meat if you want and don't just say Souldon chicken when you order or you will get the half chicken with the Souldon sauce. I don't like bones so I always order the "chicken steak".

Sides are steamed Veggie (if you're feeling healthy) or French fries (seasoned fries). And either white rice or pasta (the pasta here is 100% more tasty than any other cafe I've ever been to in SGV).

I come here for the steak menu section, can't go wrong with that. All the Chinese dishes are mediocre. Service is still Asian style if you know what I mean. Lol, decor is good and all those flat screen for sports are awesome.

I dropped my babies teething toy under the table and forgot to pick it up since we're still having dinner and didn't want to go squeeze under the table. Left the restaurant, came back the next day looking for it and no one was a help and just say it's not here anymore. Like I said, service still suck.
Also, I once pointed at the menu at the Souldon half chicken, but I said I wanted the Souldon chicken "steak". I said sorry, but I didn't want the half chicken, the lady came back and said, but you pointed at the half chicken. Duh you should know that you have 2 types of Souldon chicken since you work here everyday, and listen carefully because I said Souldon "steak". Again, service sucking.<//text>

< review>
We came here for the second time within a week because last Sunday we came here, we really liked the book xo sause seafood fried rice. The portion was  adequate and very tasty.  So we want to eat that again.  We ordered beef rice noodles along with the fried rice.  When the fried rice came, we noticed the portion was about 1/3 less than before, then the color and smell of the xo sause was not there. When I we tasted it, it tasted like the rice was barely mixed with other ingredients and not cooked with the work. It was only lukewarm.  Then came the beef rice noodles, same thing, small portion and looked closely and we asked" where's the beef?" Sound like the old Wendy's commercial.  We asked the waitress about it the answer we get is" this is how we cook at lunchtime, we have different cooks for dinner"  so we spent $23 for something we have to force ourselves to eat, otherwise it was go wasted. Needless to say, service was lousy also, could be because we didn't order drinks but ice water. Then there was only two small ice cubes in it. Will I go back there again? Guess what the answer is.< /review>

1418077929132< /time>
< Text>
Food here is good. A bit different from other HK cafes because they have their rotisserie chicken which is pretty dang good. Service is so-so but I don't exactly go here for the service. Wish it was a bit better, because servers seem to avoid your gaze when you're trying to get their attention. They serve beer which is nice, I don't see a lot of HK cafes that have beers on tap. But a recommendation for them would be to maybe chill their beer more, or actually chill their glasses so people can have cold glasses when they order pitchers of beers. Weekend dinners are usually packed so if you decide to go on those nights be prepared to wait. I've had fairly pleasant experiences while eating here each time but I've learned to go when it less crowded as service is better then.</Text>
